  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_eab0c888-8dd0-45b6-a708-d758b7927b21'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText16030314924844589001" style="display:none">Listen — Travis Coates was alive once and then he wasn’t.<br /><br />Now he’s alive again.<br /><br />Simple as that.<br /><br />The in between part is still a little fuzzy, but he can tell you that, at some point or another, his head got chopped off and shoved into a freezer in Denver, Colorado. Five years later, it was reattached to some other guy’s body, and well, here he is. Despite all logic, he’s still 16 and everything and everyone around him has changed. That includes his bedroom, his parents, his best friend, and his girlfriend. Or maybe she’s not his girlfriend anymore? That’s a bit fuzzy too.<br /><br />Looks like if the new Travis and the old Travis are ever going to find a way to exist together, then there are going to be a few more scars.<br /><br />Oh well, you only live twice.</span>

        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1174923481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15882895224974243652">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>I would say I “didn’t get” this story, but seriously . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://lunapic.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447885429ra/17061858.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The <b>idea</b> of <i>Noggin</i> was great . . . <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Everything can go from fine and dandy to dark and depressing faster than you can say ‘acute lymphoblastic leukemia.’”</i>
</b><br/><br/>When Travis Coates was diagnosed with terminal cancer as a 16-year old boy, he was offered a potential second chance . . . .<br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447885159ra/17061834.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Travis chose to roll the dice and have his head cryogenically frozen. What he didn’t plan o</span>
  <span id="freeText15882895224974243652" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>I would say I “didn’t get” this story, but seriously . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447885429ra/17061858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The <b>idea</b> of <i>Noggin</i> was great . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Everything can go from fine and dandy to dark and depressing faster than you can say ‘acute lymphoblastic leukemia.’”</i>
</b><br><br>When Travis Coates was diagnosed with terminal cancer as a 16-year old boy, he was offered a potential second chance . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447885159ra/17061834.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Travis chose to roll the dice and have his head cryogenically frozen. What he didn’t plan on was the technology moving so fast and him “waking up” a mere five years later. Here’s where the problems started for me. Like I said, the <i>idea</i> was totally original. Unfortunately, the execution left much to be desired. Travis returns to his former life expecting everything to pretty much have remained status quo. And there were <b>some</b> life lessons and quotable quotes included in the story . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“We go along with impossible things because we have to survive when life starts getting too dark.”</i>
</b><br><br>The majority of the time, though? There was an awful lot of me wanting to kick Travis in the nads. Being a person who is raising a teenager, I understand that Travis was probably waaaaaay more realistic than the average YA character. Buuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuut, in this case I needed him to not be. To begin with, Travis re-friends his former (gay) bestie, only to find out that said bestie now bats for the hetero team. I’m not even going to get into the argument about sexuality being something that can be measured on a gradient rather than set in stone, but focus on the fact that JUST ACCEPT YOUR F-ING FRIEND FOR WHO HE IS! I mean, here’s a 20-something who has a dead 16 year old thrown back in his life and is just supposed to be cool with that. Does it really matter if your gay friend is no longer gay?????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447885159ra/17061835.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Which leads us to Travis’ <b>other</b> obsession – his old girlfriend. Said old girlfriend has also aged 5 years, and although she said she’d wait forever no one <b>really</b> believed Travis would come back from the dead so she moved on and is now engaged to someone else. That’s not okay with Travis, though, and he makes it his mission to plant himself in her path as much as possible because he’s <b>positive</b> she’ll see she’s made a mistake . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447885159ra/17061836.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She’s just not that into you, Travis. And also? You’re a minor and she probably doesn’t want to be sitting across the table from Chris Hansen anytime soon.<br><br>This story had tons of potential, and the fact that it was a National Book Award finalist had me believing it was really going to be something special. Sadly I found it to be the same tired out tropes I’ve read in YA fiction a bazillion times before. <br><br><b>HOWEVER</b> my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384179384?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">TL</a> had a completely opposite reaction to this book, so maybe you’ll love it too?<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15882895224974243652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5313535777300772016">NOGGIN is headed for greatness and is without a doubt my favorite YA book. I won't go into plot or anything because that would mean getting aHEAD of ourselves since it doesn't pub until next April, but for anyone who's read WHERE THINGS COME BACK, I promise you that NOGGIN is a follow-up that will blow your head off your shoulders. <br/><br/>I've never cried reading a book before - and I've read many, many books - but there was a beautiful scene that transformed me from robot to human and that's a testame</span>
  <span id="freeText5313535777300772016" style="display:none">NOGGIN is headed for greatness and is without a doubt my favorite YA book. I won't go into plot or anything because that would mean getting aHEAD of ourselves since it doesn't pub until next April, but for anyone who's read WHERE THINGS COME BACK, I promise you that NOGGIN is a follow-up that will blow your head off your shoulders. <br /><br />I've never cried reading a book before - and I've read many, many books - but there was a beautiful scene that transformed me from robot to human and that's a testament to Corey's writing. There are so many lines in this novel that only HE could've written and they're fantastic.<br /><br />If you're a teenager or adult or robot, you'll love NOGGIN and admire how Corey manages to get into the head of his character. (Pun pun pun pun.)</span>

<div id="review_1445236950" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445236950?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=annoying-mc">annoying-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=yes-i-m-disappointed">yes-i-m-disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445236950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9699850926057058694"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447971958i/17074630._SX540_.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>DISCLAIMER</u>
</b> : Don't seek scientific accuracy because there's <b>none</b>, and, really, that's not the point. You don't believe me? Just imagine I'd ask <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4113638.John_Corey_Whaley' title='John Corey Whaley' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Corey Whaley</a> if he wanted to tell a realistic story, <i>scientifically wise</i>. <br/><br/><i>"Yeah. Sure. That's exactly why I chose to talk about a guy whose head is cut off then frozen THEN attached to someone else's body. Sure."</i> *side glances* - who is this crazy chick?<br/><br/>There's this weird thing we often use when reading scifi, called <i>
  <b>suspension of disbelief</b>
</i>.</span>
  <span id="freeText9699850926057058694" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447971958i/17074630._SX540_.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>DISCLAIMER</u>
</b> : Don't seek scientific accuracy because there's <b>none</b>, and, really, that's not the point. You don't believe me? Just imagine I'd ask <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4113638.John_Corey_Whaley" title="John Corey Whaley" rel="nofollow noopener">John Corey Whaley</a> if he wanted to tell a realistic story, <i>scientifically wise</i>. <br><br><i>"Yeah. Sure. That's exactly why I chose to talk about a guy whose head is cut off then frozen THEN attached to someone else's body. Sure."</i> *side glances* - who is this crazy chick?<br><br>There's this weird thing we often use when reading scifi, called <i>
  <b>suspension of disbelief</b>
</i>. That sums it up. *blows kiss*<br><br>▶ <b>That does not mean that I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18528439.Noggin" title="Noggin by John Corey Whaley" rel="nofollow noopener">Noggin</a>. Hell, by the end I pretty much hated it.</b> I just thought I'd point that scientific inaccuracy was by no means what bothered me. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447971958i/17074631._SX540_.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Say, you are a 16 years old guy dying from cancer. You want to come back from the dead years after with a new body? You think that's a good idea? That it must be fun to discover a whole new self? <br><br><b>Well, think again</b>. <br><br>✘ First it's so fucking <b>gross</b>. There are whole parts of yourself you have to make acquaintance with *cough* your new penis *cough*. <br><br>✘ Your friends have moved on in their lives and frankly? The whole "I return from the dead" trip is freaking them out something fierce... or so you suppose, because that's not as if they would welcome you anyway, let alone talk to you (they'll get over it, but still). Basically you took the longest nap of your life. 5 years. Except that wasn't a nap for people who loved you. They missed you. They mourned you. Then they went through the 7 phases of grief and created a new life without you. Yeah, that sucks, but hey! We can't blame them. But you, <i>YOU</i>. Think about you. <i>You</i> didn't miss them. <i>You</i> didn't move on, because HELLO, 5 min nap! <i>You</i> are stuck in a 16 years old body while they're 5 years older now.<br><br>✘ Oh, and you're a miracle (or an abomination, depending on who's talking to you). Three blessings and 24/7 covering, here's the new guy everyone is gossiping about! Just smile already. <br><br>You don't? <i>Awwww</i>. What an ungrateful little jerk you are, really. Just be happy already. <br><br><b>We can't blame Travis for being confused, messed-up, and a little angry. His behavior is pretty realistic. I know that. BUT the delusion, man. This is <u>too-much</u></b>. <br><br>*<i>Delusion is a belief held with strong conviction despite superior evidence to the contrary</i>. OR : <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447971958i/17074632._SX540_.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Albeit well-written, funny and moving at times, Travis' <s>mess</s> story was <b>incredibly frustrating</b> : after having (really) enjoyed the beginning, I wanted to submit him to an intervention pretty fast, to be honest. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448039373i/17085382._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>TRAVIS, JUST MOVE THE FUCK ON. Cate is 21. She has lived without you for 5 years. And that doesn't mean that she didn't love you before but she is <i>engaged</i> now, buddy. I'd hate for you to do something embarrass-<br><br><i>Oh, never mind</i>. Of course you're RIGHT. Of course EVERYBODY is wrong. GD.<br><br>I can't help but HATE when characters say things like <i>"I'm gonna make her change her mind. I'm gonna go all sneaky and tell her that's okay to be just friends but in fact I'll plot the end of her (happy) relationship"</i>. I CAN'T. Past is in the past. I'm sorry, but that's how I feel it. That's why even though I felt bad for him, even though I could understand why he felt that way, <b>I couldn't get past his absolute denial of everyone else's feelings</b>, especially Cate, his former girlfriend, and Kyle, his best-friend. <br><br>By the end I couldn't stand him, and his burgeoning self-loathing didn't help either. Perhaps I'm being unfair, but really, what can I say about a book where the male-lead, if not a complete asshole, is making me <i>cringe</i> so bad that I struggle to finish his story? <br><br>▶ <b>I'll give it a 2, no matter how much I enjoyed the first 20 percents</b>, no matter how original the concept is, no matter how many tears threatened to fall from my eyes in the beginning. Because, really, who enjoys a book where we only want for the MC to shut <i>the fuck</i> up? <br><br>Certainly not me. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_1070658880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070658880" />
    <a title="Neal Shusterman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5092518-neal-shusterman"><img alt="Neal Shusterman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449838p2/5092518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070658880?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neal Shusterman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neal Shusterman" href="/user/show/5092518-neal-shusterman">Neal Shusterman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070658880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer563852330851242136">Really enjoyed this one! The premise here is my kind of story -- a dying kid decides to have his head cryogenically frozen, figuring if they ever revive him, it will be in the distant future. Well, surprise, it happens five years later. He now has the buff body of some dead kid, and has to deal with that, and the fact that everyone in his life is five years older, and his parents who had mourned him, now have him back, which is weird on all fronts.<br/><br/>Having explored similar transplant-related issue</span>
  <span id="freeText563852330851242136" style="display:none">Really enjoyed this one! The premise here is my kind of story -- a dying kid decides to have his head cryogenically frozen, figuring if they ever revive him, it will be in the distant future. Well, surprise, it happens five years later. He now has the buff body of some dead kid, and has to deal with that, and the fact that everyone in his life is five years older, and his parents who had mourned him, now have him back, which is weird on all fronts.<br /><br />Having explored similar transplant-related issues in the Unwind books, it’s wonderful to see how another author handles the subject matter. I think my only criticism would be that I would have loved to have seen more of the story focus on him coming to terms with this new body, and the ambivalent emotions, instead spending so much time on the love story. I would have loved to have seen more of the family of the body donor, and the main characters coming to terms with them. But that’s the sign of a good book -- it leaves you wishing that more of the concept could have been explored.</span>
  <a data-text-id="563852330851242136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_936942151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/936942151" />
    <a title="Andrew Hicks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29779942-andrew-hicks"><img alt="Andrew Hicks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395286088p2/29779942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/936942151?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Hicks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Hicks" href="/user/show/29779942-andrew-hicks">Andrew Hicks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442458727" href="/book/show/18051349-noggin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29779942-andrew-hicks?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer936942151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6397671920486047623">When I got married in 2007, we moved 120 miles away. In 2011, we moved back. I thought my return would be the best of both worlds - I’d have my new family life and old friends back, redefined for adulthood. I walked into my old bar, the neighborhood hangout from my single years, and the same people were there, many of them sitting on the same stools, all of them doing and talking the same shit. And for me - it was obvious, immediately - it wasn’t the same. Three years later, I still haven’t gone</span>
  <span id="freeText6397671920486047623" style="display:none">When I got married in 2007, we moved 120 miles away. In 2011, we moved back. I thought my return would be the best of both worlds - I’d have my new family life and old friends back, redefined for adulthood. I walked into my old bar, the neighborhood hangout from my single years, and the same people were there, many of them sitting on the same stools, all of them doing and talking the same shit. And for me - it was obvious, immediately - it wasn’t the same. Three years later, I still haven’t gone back to that bar.<br /><br />Now imagine being Travis Coates, the protagonist/narrator of <b>
  <i>Noggin</i>
</b>. At the age of 16, with a terminal case of leukemia, Travis volunteered for a secret, sci-fi-sounding surgery. His head was cut off and cryogenically frozen. Now, five years later, feeling like he woke up from a nap, Travis regains consciousness in a hospital bed, surrounded by doctors, nurses and his parents. Travis’s head has been transplanted onto a perfectly healthy donor body. He is a miracle of modern science, and his marching orders are to go live and enjoy life again.<br /><br />So there’s this <i>
  <b>Flight of the Navigator</b>
</i>-type situation going on. For Travis, no time has passed. For his best friend Kyle and girlfriend Cate, who are now in their early 20s, it’s been a half-decade of mourning Travis and trying to go live and enjoy life again. Now, unexpectedly, he’s back.<br /><br />The wedge, aside from the natural effects of time spent apart, between Travis and Kyle stems from the fact that Kyle told him on his deathbed that he (i.e. Kyle) was gay. Now Kyle’s like, <i>Never mind that shit, meet my girlfriend.</i> Whoops... Guys, though, especially Guys in Fiction, can always work out their conflicts.<br /><br />Cate proves a tougher nut to crack. She’s engaged now, to a 25-year-old full-fledged adult. Travis’s single-minded mentality is, <i>Cate belongs with me, I’ll do what it takes to get her back</i>. And, throughout the book, that attitude never wavers - even though picking up with Cate is clearly impossible, making the situation sad, overstated, painful to observe and doomed to futility.<br /><br />Cate and Travis is the relationship the book hinges on - there are flashbacks aplenty - and they’re no <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/899856419" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor and Park</a>, but they made a pretty awesome couple back in the day. <i>
  <b>Noggin</b>
</i> is five parts Cate and Travis, three parts Travis and Kyle, two parts Travis and Hatton (Travis’s new best friend in high school, likable but essentially a Kyle clone), and one part Travis and his parents. <br /><br />There are just a couple minor supporting characters, the only significant one being Lawrence - married dude, father, and the only other person on Earth who’s been successfully brought back to life with his head on a donor body. Lawrence pops up on the phone every now and again to assure Travis that, <i>Yeah, this shit is weird</i>, and <i>Nah, nobody else could ever understand what it’s like to be us</i>.<br /><br />Author John Corey Whaley, who won the Printz Award with his 2011 debut <i>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926227082" rel="nofollow noopener">Where Things Come Back</a>
  </b>
</i>, went much more high-concept and ambitious with the premise and scope of <b>
  <i>Noggin</i>
</b>, his sophomore effort. But he scaled back the story and the characters this time. The plot itself is threadbare, though there was one revelatory twist at the two-thirds mark that I <i>really</i> didn’t see coming. <br /><br />The emotional exploration, though, is huge. These are characters you’ll empathize with individually, even when they’re at odds with each other. <b>
  <i>Noggin</i>
</b> is by no means epic, and it does meander (like <b>
  <i>Where Things Come Back</i>
</b>, it could be twice as good at half the length), but it has huge heart and winning humor. I’m eager to follow Whaley as his writing career progresses.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6397671920486047623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100336088?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100336088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11862350003213906391">A few basic facts.....<br/>It's a Young Adult book about a dying kid - *Travis* - who chooses to have his <br/>head cryogenically frozen. Five years later - he's back - alive with a fit- and taller body. <br/>To Travis, it only feels like he's been asleep for the night -- in no way does it seem like five years has gone by without him. <br/><br/>However, after Travis woke up his parents kept saying how much they missed him. <br/>It made Travis feel weird. Very weird! <br/>Everything is different ... everyONE is different.<br/><br/>Travis is</span>
  <span id="freeText11862350003213906391" style="display:none">A few basic facts.....<br />It's a Young Adult book about a dying kid - *Travis* - who chooses to have his <br />head cryogenically frozen. Five years later - he's back - alive with a fit- and taller body. <br />To Travis, it only feels like he's been asleep for the night -- in no way does it seem like five years has gone by without him. <br /><br />However, after Travis woke up his parents kept saying how much they missed him. <br />It made Travis feel weird. Very weird! <br />Everything is different ... everyONE is different.<br /><br />Travis is trying to figure out how to be ...and everyone is watching. He feels 16...but he's 21. It 'feels' like he still has a girlfriend ...but she's engaged to somebody else. <br />His parents are no longer the same. He has to deal with school, friends, and sexuality. <br />He's awkward, confused, annoying, and lovable. <br /><br />Parts of this book is very funny. Parts very sad. Mostly it's thought provoking. <br />I actually thought about the five years Travis was asleep. I tried to imagine the way life took shape - and changed dramatically for his parents. <br />Also...just trying to imagine 'returning' to life ( after being frozen), is mind blowing. The adjustments would be astronomical. <br /><br />John Corey Whaley's writing style flows naturally. The characters seem authentic... and the humor understated. I adored it!!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11862350003213906391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17906886326585409462">*edited somewhat 11-1-15 with quotes and extra thoughts*<br/><br/><i>“Maybe we all just exist, all versions of us exist at times, and we have to figure out a way to get to each of them, to find each one and tell that version that it's okay, that it's all just the way it works, a concept too powerful to ignore but too complicated to explain.”</i><br/>--<br/><i>“No matter how often you see or talk to someone, no matter how much you know them or don't know them, you always fill up some space in their lives that can't ever be re</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17906886326585409462" style="display:none">*edited somewhat 11-1-15 with quotes and extra thoughts*<br /><br /><i>“Maybe we all just exist, all versions of us exist at times, and we have to figure out a way to get to each of them, to find each one and tell that version that it's okay, that it's all just the way it works, a concept too powerful to ignore but too complicated to explain.”</i><br />--<br /><i>“No matter how often you see or talk to someone, no matter how much you know them or don't know them, you always fill up some space in their lives that can't ever be replaced the right way again once you leave it.” </i><br />----<br />A tale you have to suspend belief for on one aspect but an interesting one with that at first is slightly creepy but it didn't take me long to sink into the story.<br /><br />I couldn't imagine making the decision Travis did, not knowing for sure if you would come back and adjusting to everything being different when you aren't. <br /><br /><i>“We all get lots of people. And maybe we don’t always get to have them the exact way we want them, but if we can figure out a way to compromise, you know, then we can keep them all.” </i><br /><br /><i>“Okay, so first we get you a new computer and then a Facebook page. Priorities, you know," he said, typing in Kyle's password.<br /><br />"What would I do without you--"<br /><br />"Found her," he interrupted. "She's at Carrie's OK Bar. It's downtown."<br /><br />"What the hell is Carrie's OK Bar?"<br /><br />"It's a karaoke bar. Travis, come on."<br /><br />"Wait, how do you know she's there?"<br /><br />"She checked in there about twenty minutes ago."<br /><br />"What does that mean?"<br /><br />"Oh. Right. Since you left, it's become very important that we all constantly know each other's thoughts, locations, and birthdays."<br /><br />"That's really stupid. Except for in this one very specific situation. I can't go if her fiancé's there, though. That would be too weird."<br /><br />"He's not."<br /><br />"How do you know?"<br /><br />"Because she put 'Girls' Night' with about five exclamation points after it."<br /><br />"Are people just asking to be murdered?"<br /><br />"Pretty much. So are we going?” </i><br /><br />One of my favorite bits was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when everyone, including the Doctors and Nurses, celebrated every holiday at the same time for Travis. It was so sweet! Bittersweet and moving, with a few funny moments, one moment near the end with the Easter part (with Kate and Kyle reading memories from the eggs) had me tearing up and smiling. <br /><br />“It's a real shame. I like how people act on holidays. Everyone just seems . . . I don't know-- lighter, maybe. Like they're allowed to have fun all day long and eat anything they want and do silly things, and no one cares because, hey, it's a holiday, so why not?”  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Travis'quest to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[get Kate back  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was a little annoying at times. I understood his position somewhat but I was hoping he would wise up/move on (right phrases?)soon. His grand gesture of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[proposing to Kate in the coffee shop <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was misguided and crazy but oddly sweet in its own way. I was actually 'yelling' at the audiobook to Travis not to do it haha.<br /><br />Hatten (sp? since I don't have the hardcover) was a riot :). I was glad he was a genuine friend to Travis.<br /><br />A moment in the video arcade had me wanting to give Travis a big hug.<br /><br />In some places I thought it could have gone deeper into the concept but I had fun reading it :).<br /><br />Narrator for audiobook - 5 stars</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100296782?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100296782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14336086356742725886">I'd rate this 4.5, maybe 4.75 stars.<br/><br/>One of the things I love so much about reading is what different books do for me. Some entertain, some manipulate my emotions (this is not necessarily a negative), some teach, some infuriate, and some make me think. I love when a book surprises me and does more than I expect. Such was the case with John Corey Whaley's spectacular second novel, Noggin. I enjoyed it tremendously (despite its offbeat premise) and it really made me think.<br/><br/>Travis Coates was a gravel</span>
  <span id="freeText14336086356742725886" style="display:none">I'd rate this 4.5, maybe 4.75 stars.<br /><br />One of the things I love so much about reading is what different books do for me. Some entertain, some manipulate my emotions (this is not necessarily a negative), some teach, some infuriate, and some make me think. I love when a book surprises me and does more than I expect. Such was the case with John Corey Whaley's spectacular second novel, Noggin. I enjoyed it tremendously (despite its offbeat premise) and it really made me think.<br /><br />Travis Coates was a gravely ill 16-year-old who was tired of dying, but he didn't want to keep living the way he was. He and his family agreed to participate in an experimental program in which his head (the only part of his body not riddled with the cancer that was killing him) was removed from his body and, when medical and technological advances made it possible, it would be attached to another donor's body. Deep down inside, everyone had a feeling this would never happen, but it was a good thing to imagine occurring years into the future.<br /><br />One morning Travis woke up, his parents by his side, to find that his head had been reattached to another teenager's body (a better body, if anyone's counting). For Travis, it only seemed like a few hours had passed since he said goodbye to his family, his best friend, Kyle, and his girlfriend, Cate, but for everyone else, it was five years later. Five years in which so much had changed.<br /><br />"I want to tell you a story about how you can suddenly wake up to find yourself living a life you were never supposed to live. It could happen to you, just like it happened to me, and you could try to get back the life you think you deserve to be living. Just like I did."<br /><br />Travis has to return to his high school and repeat sophomore year. (While he should be 21, his body and his mind are still 16, and he didn't get enough credits while he was sick to become a junior.) Beyond everyone wanting to get a look at his really cool scar where they attached his head to the other boy's body, it's weird being there without Kyle and Cate, although he is able to make a new friend.<br /><br />But as similar as that aspect of his life is, things are really different where Kyle and Cate are concerned, as their lives moved on, much differently than Travis would have expected. Travis can't seem to understand why they can't seem to pick things up where they left off, and runs the risk of alienating the people who matter the most to him. It's truly hard to reconcile his gratitude at being able to have another chance to live with his frustration that his life can't be the way he wants it to be.<br /><br />Noggin is tremendously thought-provoking, because while the procedure that gave Travis a new lease on life is certainly difficult to grasp, it raises some interesting questions. If you thought a person you lost would come back to you, should you keep your life in a holding pattern until it was confirmed that it won't happen? What obligation do we have to those we leave behind? If this procedure existed, should it be used, or is it one step too far?<br /><br />I really loved this book. I loved the fact that Travis wasn't any wiser than he was before he died, and if anything, he's more confused. I loved all of the characters and how they were flawed, just like real life. And I love the way Whaley tells a story, which is just one reason why his previous book, Where Things Come Back, was one of my favorite books of 2012.<br /><br />If you can get past the procedure on which this book hinges, you'll really enjoy this, and it will move you if you've ever had to face the loss of someone you wish could still be with you. As Travis says, "It made me realize that no matter how often you see or talk to someone, no matter how much you know them or don't know them, you always fill up some space in their lives that can't ever be replaced the right way again once you leave it."<br /><br />Noggin might be that way for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14336086356742725886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16760153355249783605" style="display:none">4.5<br /><br />I just finished this a second ago and I really don't know how to rate it! My thoughts are all over the place.<br /><br />It was a book that made me think. The entire thing was one big what if? There were so many lines that really hit the nail on the head about dealing with loss and grieving, and learning to move on. Powerful stuff.<br /><br />But at the same time, all these powerful thing were said but I feel like I didn't get to see them happen. There was very little plot movement in this book and I absolutely 100% understand why that was so, but by the end it still felt so stagnant and incomplete. Not just with the main storyline but with secondary storylines as well. I wanted some semblance of an idea about how things would go from there, but didn't feel that I got that.<br /><br />Still, I genuinely read this book in one sitting. I couldn't stop reading, the idea was just so fascinating. I really fell into Travis' world.</span>

<div id="review_848666015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848666015" />
    <a title="Debby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8677900-debby"><img alt="Debby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496523199p2/8677900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/848666015?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debby" href="/user/show/8677900-debby">Debby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442458727" href="/book/show/18051349-noggin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8677900-debby?shelf=books-that-linger">books-that-linger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8677900-debby?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8677900-debby?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8677900-debby?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8677900-debby?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8677900-debby?shelf=sold-or-gave-away">sold-or-gave-away</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer848666015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1976641087323246182"><b>4 stars</b><br/><br/>When I was offered <i>Noggin</i> for review, I had absolutely no idea what to expect. From the blurb it just sounded unique and sort of weird. With the head cut off element, I thought it would be a bizarre kind of sci-fi, but nope. This book surprised me in the best possible way.<br/><br/><i>Noggin</i> is actually <i>sort of</i> a cancer book. It centers on Travis Coates who, indeed, has his head cut off - but for a medical reason. He had a terminal form of cancer that had destroyed his body - except for his head. Know</span>
  <span id="freeText1976641087323246182" style="display:none"><b>4 stars</b><br><br>When I was offered <i>Noggin</i> for review, I had absolutely no idea what to expect. From the blurb it just sounded unique and sort of weird. With the head cut off element, I thought it would be a bizarre kind of sci-fi, but nope. This book surprised me in the best possible way.<br><br><i>Noggin</i> is actually <i>sort of</i> a cancer book. It centers on Travis Coates who, indeed, has his head cut off - but for a medical reason. He had a terminal form of cancer that had destroyed his body - except for his head. Knowing he had no other options, he consented to participate in a new medical procedure. His head would be cut off and cryogenically frozen until such time as technology had advanced enough to allow him to survive reattachment to another body. He first expects that he would wake up far in the future, but instead he wakes up 5 years later: just long enough for his family, girlfriend and friends to have moved on, but not long enough for him to be able to let them go entirely, as for him no time had passed at all.<br><br>I honestly was not expecting that kind of story from the blurb, but it just instantly drew me in. I'm not the type of person who often goes for sickness <i>or</i> grief stories, because I find it hard to connect. But here the connection was instantaneous, mostly because Travis has such a refreshing voice. It was really fluid and easy to understand his thoughts, to be drawn into his mind and sympathize with his story. He has a wry kind of humor that pops out at <i>just</i> the right times and puts a smirk on your face despite his circumstances.<br><br>So the book tells Travis's story of coming back to life with much fanfare to the world as a medical miracle interspersed with flashbacks to show how his former life ended. Tons of emotions abound. Honestly, there were moments when I had tears in my eyes because of the beautiful bond Travis had with his family, his girlfriend Cate, and his best friend, Kyle. This book is mostly about the relationships between these characters, all of which are rather strained because of the circumstances. Everyone wants to move on, but nobody really knows how. Strangely there's no handbook on what to do when your son/(ex-)boyfriend/best friend comes back to life. And slowly it becomes obvious just how big of an effect Travis's presence (and absence) had on all of them. I really felt touched by their stories and basically loved all of the characters, including Travis's new friend, Hatton. Their relationships are beautiful, and they all give each other the reality checks they need.<br><br>I was seriously enjoying this and was super engrossed, but in my opinion, the story trailed off in the end. I didn't feel like the ending was that strong, and I was rather frustrated with Travis and some of the choices he made. While it sort of fit the trend of his desperation and clinging to his former life, I would have liked to see more growth. However, I can also imagine that this is a more realistic take on how someone in such a situation would truly react.<br><br>Ultimately, <i>Noggin</i> is a really unique take on an aftermath of cancer story. It's a book that really makes you think about your own life, choices and relationships, and about the passage of time. When I finished, I felt sort of fragile. I needed to just lie in bed for a while and digest - and it's very rare that a book has that kind of effect on me. So while I didn't feel like the ending was that strong, it did leave a mark on me as a reader. And that is excellent. For what it's worth, I think this would be a brilliant book for a book club, because it definitely fosters discussion.<br><br><b>
  <i>Summing Up:</i>
</b><br><br>This is a strange little book, but I cannot stress enough how glad I am that it found its way into my hands. While it's a story that's a bit out of my comfort zone, it worked out extremely well. I loved this unique premise, with its awesome characters, beautiful relationships, and refreshing voice. It's a book that will linger on in your mind for days. And personally, I'm betting it will beg me for a reread at some point.<br><br><b>
  <i>GIF it to me straight!</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394618082ra/8877659.gif" alt="giphy324" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Recommended To:</i>
</b><br><br>Fans of character-driven stories dealing with the consequences of life and death, and/or, potentially, fans of <a href="http://www.snugglyoranges.com/2013/01/book-review-fault-in-our-stars-by-john/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>.<br><br><br><i>*ARC was provided by <a href="http://abc.nl/" rel="nofollow noopener">ABC</a> in exchange for an honest review. Thank you! This does not affect my opinion of the book or the contents of the review.</i><br><br><a href="http://www.snugglyoranges.com/2014/03/arc-book-review-noggin-john-corey-whaley/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385545769i/7172215.png" alt="Snuggly Oranges - YA Book Blog" width="200" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_998526847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/998526847" />
    <a title="Gabby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby"><img alt="Gabby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482222518p2/26560207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998526847?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabby" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby">Gabby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=liked-it">liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=love-the-concept">love-the-concept</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-one-day">read-in-one-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998526847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16625090648123876955">I loved this book so much more than I was expecting. After reading the synopsis I was really intrigued and I was curious to see how this story would unfold. It did not disappoint at all. One minute i was literally laughing out loud (which is rare for me to actually do while reading) and the next I was crying. I couldn't believe how emotional some of these scenes were for me, and how attached I got to these characters. <i>All</i> of the characters in this book are well developed: Travis, Cate, Kyle, eve</span>
  <span id="freeText16625090648123876955" style="display:none">I loved this book so much more than I was expecting. After reading the synopsis I was really intrigued and I was curious to see how this story would unfold. It did not disappoint at all. One minute i was literally laughing out loud (which is rare for me to actually do while reading) and the next I was crying. I couldn't believe how emotional some of these scenes were for me, and how attached I got to these characters. <i>All</i> of the characters in this book are well developed: Travis, Cate, Kyle, even Travis's parents are well developed characters, which I wasn't expecting. This is a story about life and death and grief, but also a story about what it means to be alive.<br /><br />I stayed up till 2am reading this book because I couldn't put it down and I was enjoying it so much. Travis is a very relatable character. It's just the way he thinks, the way this book is written that makes Travis such a relatable character. <i>"But in that moment I understood what they say about nostalgia, that no matter if you're thinking of something good or bad, it always leaves you a little emptier afterward."</i> I highlighted that quote because I completely agree and I thought it was so beautifully said. John Corey Whaley has a beautiful way with words, and an incredible sense of humor. I loved Hatton's character, I could not stop laughing every time he opened his mouth. I also really loved the relationship between Travis and Kyle because you could tell they really cared about each other and wanted each other to be happy.<br /><br />I think the idea that you could wake up 5 years later and have your head attached to another human being is terrifying, but also amazing. The fact that Travis got a second chance at life is so fascinating, but I like that this book dives into the problems that also happen in a situation like this. because yes, it is a miracle, but Travis feels like he is left out and has missed growing up with his friends, and he doesn't understand what has happened within his own family.<br /><br />The one problem I had with this book was Cate's character. I don't know why, she just bugged me. Maybe it was because she constantly lead him on, even though she was engaged, and then she would get pissed at him for trying anything with her. I think it was a cool plot point to have his previous girlfriend be engaged to another guy when he wakes up, but I also thought she took up so much of Travis's time. It felt a little repetitive at times with Travis trying to be with her and her leading him on, just to reject him later. I understand that Travis was a little naive, but I admired his optimism at the same time. I just wish Cate wouldn't have led him on so much. I also think it ended kind of awkwardly between Cate and Travis because to me it feel like nothing had been resolved between them. At least not in the way I wanted. However, i will agree with what Cate said, when she said everyone has soul mates for different times in their lives. I agree because it's hard to believe in just one soul mate. I think we have several soul mates at different times in our lives, and that's okay. I think our soul mate at the time is whoever makes us happiest in the world at that moment, and if that changes several years later, that's okay too. But I did think the ending in general was kind of awkward and I didn't really understand why it ended the way it did. I was expecting it to end beautifully and give me a positive outlook on life, but then it just kind of ended. I felt like maybe there should have been an extra chapter at the end just to sum everything up.<br /><br />Other than that, I really enjoyed Noggin. This book somewhat reminded me of "Winger" by Andrew Smith and "Everyday" by David Levithan. It reminded me of Winger because of the humor, and Everyday because of his constant desire to be with this one girl. I enjoyed those books as well and this will only add to the collection of books I love. I can't wait to read other books by John Corey Whaley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16625090648123876955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_938079587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938079587" />
    <a title="Ken Shindle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10853632-ken-shindle"><img alt="Ken Shindle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483130845p2/10853632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938079587?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Shindle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Shindle" href="/user/show/10853632-ken-shindle">Ken Shindle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938079587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3012889210628244313"><i>Noggin</i> is a disappointing follow-up to Whaley's thought-provoking, well-written <i>Where Things Come Back</i>; it's a predictable story filled with banalities, shallow characters, and completely unbelievable dialogue. I hate being hard on a book quite obviously written for children, but I've come to expect a lot more from YA literature.<br/><br/><i>Noggin</i> reads like an elementary school version of <i>The Great Gatsby</i> (though Whaley adds curses, I guess, to make his story seem more mature): a male protagonist reemerges</span>
  <span id="freeText3012889210628244313" style="display:none"><i>Noggin</i> is a disappointing follow-up to Whaley's thought-provoking, well-written <i>Where Things Come Back</i>; it's a predictable story filled with banalities, shallow characters, and completely unbelievable dialogue. I hate being hard on a book quite obviously written for children, but I've come to expect a lot more from YA literature.<br /><br /><i>Noggin</i> reads like an elementary school version of <i>The Great Gatsby</i> (though Whaley adds curses, I guess, to make his story seem more mature): a male protagonist reemerges among family and friends after a five year absence during which his head was attached to another man's body, and he's desperate for everyone to act as if nothing has changed while he was gone. Travis longs for former beau Cate just as Gatsby longs for the alluring Daisy Buchanan; Travis, too, reacts angrily to assertions that the past is gone forever just as Gatsby does. I kept waiting, in fact, for one of Travis Coates's friends to yell at him, as Nick Carraway yells at Gatsby in Fitzgerald's masterpiece, that he "can't repeat the past" and for Travis to yell back, "Can't repeat the past? Why, of course you can!" The theme works in <i>Gatsby</i> because of Fitzgerald's ability to craft a powerful love story and to make the titular character one on which readers can take pity and one who shows us all the dangers of nostalgia; it fails here because Travis Coates and his commonplace story are so woefully underdeveloped. <br /><br />There is a good book somewhere hidden within in the plot of <i>Noggin</i>. There are fascinating ethical and moral issues Whaley could've explored in his book: was Travis ever legally dead? is the surgery Travis undergoes a morally defensible one? what happens to a family that experiences a retroactively unnecessary grieving process? would it have been easier for those with whom Travis was closest to simply stay in his limbo? Instead, Whaley leaves these conversations for the "grown ups," only ever addressed on nightly news broadcasts that Travis tunes out.<br /><br />Whaley, too, has a horrible habit of telling his reader why something should be emotionally impactful <i>after</i> his opportunity for that emotional impact has passed. "Travis cried over the loss of two chairs from an old theatre that he set up in his room before his surgery," Whaley seems to say. "Now, let me tell you why those chairs were so important to him." It didn't work for me as I tried desperately to find something in which I could be invested.<br /><br />I'll read Whaley's next book, for sure, because I was so impressed with his debut, but <i>Noggin</i> left me scratching my head.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3012889210628244313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
